[1714] "Ah, Sonya. They had a falling out years ago and have been estranged ever since."

[1716] "Yes, she married a man - what was his name -"
[1717] "Stanfordtis."
[1718] "That's him, Dimetri Stanfordtis. Randall always thought he was a fraud. The two men never liked each other from the start. But Sonya was madly in love with him and wanted to marry him. I couldn't understand why she couldn't just marry him. Men's views on such things are always so strange. Sonya was no longer a little girl - she was twenty-five, and she knew what she was doing. [1719] "Did their rift ever resolve?"
[1720] "No. Randall and Sonya never got along well. She hated him for trying to stop the marriage. She said, 'Well, you're so unreasonable! I'll never speak to you again!'"
[1721] "But it wasn't like that for you, was it?"
[1722] Bella smiled. "Eighteen months later, I received a letter from her. I remember it was from Budapest, but she didn't leave an address. She told me to tell Randall that she was extremely happy and had a pair of twins."
[1723] "Did she tell you their names?"
[1724] Bella smiled again. "She said they were born just after noon — she planned to name them Pip and Emma [2]. Of course, these names could have been a joke."
[1725] "Did you hear from her again after that?"
[1726] "No. She said she and her husband were going to take their little ones to America for a while. And then I never heard from her again…"
[1727] "Do you happen to still have that letter?"
[1728] "No, I'm afraid I don't. I told Randall about the letter, and he just grumbled, 'There's always going to be a day when she regrets marrying that guy.' That's all he said about it. We had actually forgotten about her. She was out of our lives…"
[1729] "But Mr. Goddard left his property to her children in case Miss Blacklock passed away before you?"
[1730] "Oh, that was my idea. When he told me about the will, I said, 'What if I die before her?' He was surprised. I said, 'Well, I know Blacklock is as strong as a horse, and I'm a delicate flower - but you know, accidents can happen, and squeaky doors last longer.' Then he said, 'There's no one else - none at all.' So I said, 'Well, there's Sonya.' He immediately retorted, 'Let that guy have my money? No way!' I said, 'Well, then give it to her children. Pip and Emma, and there might be more by now.' So he grumbled and grumbled, but he added that in."
[1731] "Since then," Corrodick said slowly, "you haven't heard anything about your sister-in-law and her children?"
[1732] "No – they may be dead, or – anywhere."
[1733] They might be in Chipping Cheddar, Corrodick thought.
[1734] Bella Goddard seemed to read his mind, and her eyes widened in surprise. She said, "Don't let them hurt Blanche. Blanche is a good person – very good – you must stop them from hurting her –"
[1735] Her voice suddenly cut off. Corrodick saw a gray shadow appear in the corners of her mouth and eyes.
[1736] "You are tired," he said, "I must leave."
[1737] She nodded.
[1738] "Call Mac[3] in," she whispered, "Yes...I am tired..."
[1739] Her hand weakly moved. "Take care of Blairch...never let anything happen to her...take care of her..."
[1740] "I will do my best, Mrs. Goodlady." He stood up and walked towards the door.
[1741] Her voice was so faint it was like a thread, coming from behind him...
[1742] "Time is short... Before I die... She is in danger... Take care of her..."
[1743] As he went out, the MacLane nurse passed him and he spoke uneasily, "I hope I haven't caused her any harm."
[1744] "Oh, I don't think so, Mr. Corrado," she said, "I told you she would suddenly tire."
[1745] Later, he asked the nurse, "There's just one thing I didn't get to ask Mrs. Goddard... Do you happen to have any photos of her from the past? If so, I'd like to..."
[1746] She interrupted him.
[1747] "I'm afraid there's nothing like that. All her personal documents and belongings were kept in the London mansion during the early days of the war. Mrs. Goddard was very ill at the time. Everything saved there was destroyed during the Blitz. Mrs. Goddard was very upset about losing so many personal mementos and family documents. I'm afraid there's nothing left here."
[1748] So that's that, thought Corrado.
[1749] However, he felt the trip was not in vain. The ghosts of Pip and Emma, the twin siblings, were not mere figments.
[1750] Corrado thought. "There are a pair of siblings raised in Europe. Mrs. Goddard was a wealthy woman when she married, but money dispersed quickly in Europe at that time. During the war, economic fluctuations were very unusual. These two young people, the children of the man with the criminal record, were left almost penniless in England. What would they do? Look for the whereabouts of all their wealthy relatives. Their uncle, a wealthy millionaire, had passed away. So the first thing they would do is look for the will to see if they or their mother happened to inherit the money. They went to the law firm and learned the contents of the will. Then they may have also learned about Miss Letitia Blacklock, who is still alive. They inquired about the situation of Mrs. Randall Goddard, the widow. She was a sick woman living in Scotland and they learned she was not long for this world. If Miss Letitia Blacklock died before her, they would inherit a large fortune. So what would they do next?"
[1751] Cora Dedek continued to ponder: "They won't go to Scotland. They'll find out where Miss Letitia Blacklock is living now and then go there – but not under their real identities… They'll go together – or separately? Emma… I really want to know… Pip and Emma, if either of them isn't in Chipping Cleghorn, I'll eat my hat…"

He would put on airs of being a wealthy man and pay for the first term's tuition, then disappear for a year or two, leaving me with the nuns. There wasn't, meaning there was nothing directly given to me. I investigated his widow and found out she had become an old woman, kept alive by drugs, but nearing the end of her life. Frankly, it seemed like you were my best bet. You were going to inherit a huge fortune, and as far as I know, you have no heirs to inherit it.
